`<!--End Abstract-->`{=html}

:::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::: Fulltext
[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB35 .pagebreak aria-label="35"
role="doc-pagebreak" title="35"}The emergence of **Agentic
AI**[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm1} represents more than an
incremental improvement in artificial
[intelligence]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm2}---it marks a
**paradigm shift** in how machines reason, act, and collaborate. We are
moving from systems that merely **respond to prompts** to those that can
**initiate actions**, pursue goals, and adapt to new situations
autonomously. This shift brings with it both immense opportunity and
significant complexity.

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par3 .Para}
At the heart of this transformation is the distinction between **AI
agents** and **Agentic AI systems**:

::: UnorderedList
- **AI agents** are software entities designed to operate in specific
  environments. They perceive inputs, process data, and perform actions
  toward predefined goals. While they may include some level of
  automation or decision-making, they typically follow narrow,
  deterministic paths---like [robotic process automation
  (RPA)]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm3} scripts or chatbot flows.

- []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB36 .pagebreak aria-label="36"
  role="doc-pagebreak" title="36"}**Agentic AI**, by contrast, involves
  systems that exhibit **goal-directed behavior**, **contextual
  awareness**, and the ability to **reason across multiple steps or
  tools**. These systems are not just reactive---they are **proactive**,
  capable of determining what needs to be done, planning how to do it,
  and evaluating the outcome. Agentic AI systems can dynamically adapt
  to new data, change strategies mid-task, and collaborate with humans
  or other agents to solve complex problems.
:::
::::

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par6 .Para}
This added autonomy has profound architectural implications. Agentic
systems don't operate in isolation---they require structured memory to
track long-term context, reasoning engines to plan actions, dynamic
toolchains to execute diverse tasks, and observability mechanisms to
ensure trust and control. Building such systems demands more than
plugging in an LLM API---it requires an **intentional, modular
architecture** that supports

::: UnorderedList
- Real-time decision-making and contextual adaptation

- Secure integration with enterprise tools and APIs

- Coordination among multiple agents with shared goals

- Transparent logging, monitoring, and human oversight
:::
::::

In enterprise environments, this architecture must also be **scalable,
explainable, and compliant**. You can't afford black-box decisions in
high-stakes domains like finance, law, or healthcare. And you can't
tolerate brittle systems that collapse under real-world complexity.

This chapter lays the foundation for building such systems. We\'ll
explore the **architectural principles, patterns, and components** that
enable Agentic AI at scale---drawing from both cloud-native practices
and emerging agent orchestration frameworks. Whether you\'re building a
[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB37 .pagebreak aria-label="37"
role="doc-pagebreak" title="37"}decision support agent for analysts, a
knowledge navigator for enterprise search, or a multi-agent platform for
business process automation, this chapter is your **blueprint for
designing intelligent, resilient, and production-grade AI systems.**

:::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec1 .section .Section1 .RenderAsSection1 aria-labelledby="Sec1Heading"}
## [2.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Why Architecture Matters for Agentic AI {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec1Heading .Heading}

The transition from automation to autonomy doesn't just introduce new
[capabilities]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm4}---it **redefines the
entire system design philosophy**. Traditional AI agents are rule-bound
and reactive: they follow predefined scripts or respond to constrained
inputs. Their behavior is predictable but brittle, and their usefulness
is bounded by the tasks they were explicitly programmed to perform.

**Agentic AI**, by contrast, operates in open-ended environments. These
systems pursue goals rather than execute scripts. They assess
situations, select tools, reason across multiple steps, adapt to
changing contexts, and decide **when to act, when to wait, and when to
ask for help**. This autonomy is powerful---but it's also
**architecturally demanding**.

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par15 .Para}
To enable such behavior, Agentic AI systems require a set of
foundational architectural
[capabilities]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm5}, including

::: UnorderedList
- **Persistent memory** to retain context across tasks, sessions, and
  workflows---not just short-term recall but structured, queryable
  knowledge

- **Planning and reasoning modules** to support multi-step,
  goal-directed behavior and conditional logic over time

- **Tool orchestration** to interface with APIs, databases, simulators,
  or physical systems, enabling agents to perform real-world tasks

- []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB38 .pagebreak aria-label="38"
  role="doc-pagebreak" title="38"}**Perception and feedback loops** to
  monitor outcomes, verify effects, and adapt plans based on
  observations and updated context

- **Security and access governance** to enforce fine-grained control
  over what actions an agent can perform, especially when invoking
  external systems
:::
::::

But raw capability is not enough. These systems must also be
**explainable**, **auditable**, and
**resilient**[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm6}---especially in
enterprise and regulated environments where stakes are high, compliance
is strict, and trust is essential.

Without the right architecture, Agentic AI becomes unstable or
unmanageable. Models drift, workflows collapse under complexity,
observability breaks down, and errors become hard to trace or correct.
You can't scale intelligent behavior on top of **ad hoc pipelines or
opaque black boxes**.

That's why **architecture is not just implementation detail---it's
strategic infrastructure**. It enables you to build agents that are not
only smart, but **trustworthy, adaptive, and production-ready**.

In this chapter, we'll explore the core patterns and design principles
that power Agentic AI---from managing memory and tool use to
orchestrating multi-agent workflows and ensuring observability. Whether
you're designing a customer support agent, a decision assistant, or a
multi-role enterprise AI platform, a strong architectural baseline is
what turns prototypes into production-grade intelligence.

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec2 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec2Heading"}
### [2.1.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}From Task Automation to Intelligent Agency {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec2Heading .Heading}

For decades, enterprises have relied on [traditional
automation]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm7}---scripts, [robotic
process automation (RPA)]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm8}, and
rule-based engines---to accelerate repetitive workflows. While these
systems excel at predictable, linear
[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB39 .pagebreak aria-label="39"
role="doc-pagebreak" title="39"}processes (e.g., invoice processing,
data entry), they falter when faced with ambiguity, dynamic inputs, or
multi-step decision chains.

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par26 .Para}
Agentic AI represents the next
[evolution]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm9}: systems that not only
**react**, but **proactively plan**, **reason**, and **execute** complex
tasks autonomously. By embedding [large language models
(LLMs)]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm10} and adaptive workflows,
agentic systems can

::: UnorderedList
- **Interpret unstructured inputs** such as natural language, sensor
  feeds, or API responses.

- **Formulate hypotheses** and evaluate trade-offs in real time.

- **Orchestrate downstream tools**---APIs, databases, and
  microservices---to fulfill objectives end to end.
:::
::::

This shift---from static automation to intelligent agency---unlocks new
capabilities in areas such as dynamic pricing, real-time supply-chain
rerouting, and autonomous customer support.

<figure id="Fig1" class="Figure">
<div id="631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_MO1" class="MediaObject">
<img src="images/631522_1_En_2_Chapter/631522_1_En_2_Fig1_HTML.jpg"
class="ImageStyle4"

</div></figcaption>
</figure>

[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB40 .pagebreak aria-label="40"
role="doc-pagebreak" title="40"}**Callout:** "Automation optimizes
execution; agency optimizes decision-making."
:::::

:::::::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec3 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec3Heading"}
### [2.1.2 ]{.HeadingNumber}Business Drivers and Adoption Metrics {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec3Heading .Heading}

Agentic AI is swiftly moving from concept to reality, with more
enterprises embracing its potential to transform business
[operations]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm13}. Capgemini's Global
AI Report reveals compelling adoption trends and highlights the growing
importance of intelligent agents in modern enterprises. Here's a
breakdown of the key drivers and adoption metrics.

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec4 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec4Heading"}
#### [2.1.2.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Key Business Drivers {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec4Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par33 .Para}
::: UnorderedList
- **Efficiency and productivity:** Agentic AI automates not only routine
  tasks but also complex decision-making processes, freeing up human
  resources for higher-value work. AI agents can operate 24/7,
  significantly boosting
  productivity.[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm14}

- **Real-time decision-making:** Businesses need to respond faster than
  ever to changing market conditions. Agentic AI enables instant,
  data-driven decisions, helping companies stay agile in dynamic
  environments.

- **Personalization at scale:** By analyzing vast amounts of customer
  data, AI agents can provide tailored recommendations and personalized
  experiences that drive customer satisfaction and loyalty.

- **Cost reduction and risk mitigation:** AI agents reduce errors, cut
  manual interventions, and enhance compliance. Their ability to
  automate compliance tasks also helps organizations adhere to
  regulatory requirements.

- []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB41 .pagebreak aria-label="41"
  role="doc-pagebreak" title="41"}**Competitive advantage:**
  Organizations using Agentic AI can outpace competitors by responding
  more quickly to customer needs, optimizing operations, and driving
  innovation through intelligent automation.
:::
::::
:::::

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec5 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec5Heading"}
#### [2.1.2.2 ]{.HeadingNumber}Adoption Metrics {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec5Heading .Heading}

[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm15}Agentic AI---autonomous systems
capable of reasoning, decision-making, and executing complex tasks
without constant human oversight---is rapidly moving from
experimentation to enterprise adoption. No longer confined to research
labs or innovation pilots, these intelligent agents are beginning to
reshape core business
operations.[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm16}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par40 .Para}
A 2024 global survey by Capgemini, involving over 1,100 executives
across more than 20 industries, underscores this shift (ZDNET (October
9, 2024)). The data reveals not just a trend, but a tipping point:

::: UnorderedList
- **Ten percent of enterprises have already deployed AI agents**,
  primarily in high-impact areas such as customer service automation,
  fraud detection, and operational triage. These early adopters are
  seeing measurable gains in speed, accuracy, and scalability.

- **Over 50% plan to implement agentic systems by 2025**, signaling that
  intelligent autonomy is no longer a niche investment but a mainstream
  strategic priority.

- **By 2028, adoption is expected to reach 82%**, with enterprises
  integrating agentic capabilities into critical workflows across
  departments---from finance and compliance to supply chain and HR.
:::
::::

This momentum reflects a [broader
realization]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm17}: traditional
automation has plateaued, and the next leap in operational efficiency,
adaptability, and intelligence will be driven by systems that can think,
act, and learn on their own.
:::::

::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec6 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec6Heading"}
#### [2.1.2.3 ]{.HeadingNumber}Looking Ahead {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec6Heading .Heading}

[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB42 .pagebreak aria-label="42"
role="doc-pagebreak" title="42"}As AI adoption expands, enterprises will
continue leveraging [intelligent
agents]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm18} to optimize workflows,
enhance decision-making, and unlock new business models. The next wave
of adoption will see even more sophisticated AI systems across
industries, including healthcare, finance, and retail, with a growing
emphasis on responsible AI governance to ensure compliance with evolving
regulations.
:::
::::::::::

:::::::::::::::::::::::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec7 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec7Heading"}
### [2.1.3 ]{.HeadingNumber}Key Architectural Challenges in the Enterprise {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec7Heading .Heading}

Architecting Agentic AI systems within an enterprise requires a careful
balance of various factors, each contributing to the overall
functionality, security, and efficiency of the system. The following are
some of the most critical architectural
[challenges]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm19} that need to be
addressed when integrating AI agents into enterprise environments.

:::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec8 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec8Heading"}
#### [2.1.3.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Integration Complexity {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec8Heading .Heading}

One of the first hurdles in deploying Agentic AI at scale is the
[complexity]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm20} of integrating with
existing enterprise systems. Most enterprises rely on systems such as
[Enterprise Resource Planning
(ERP)]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm21}, [Customer Relationship
Management (CRM)]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm22}, and data lakes
to manage large volumes of business-critical data. However, exposing
these systems securely to AI agents can be a challenge. High-throughput
APIs are needed to allow AI systems to interact with these back-end
systems, but this introduces potential security risks.

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec9 .section .Section4 .RenderAsSection4 aria-labelledby="Sec9Heading"}
##### [2.1.3.1.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Key Considerations {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec9Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par48 .Para}
::: UnorderedList
- []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB43 .pagebreak aria-label="43"
  role="doc-pagebreak" title="43"}**Security risks:** Integrating
  external AI systems with core enterprise systems creates new attack
  vectors, making it critical to implement robust authentication and
  authorization protocols. Any API exposed to the AI system must be
  secured, and sensitive data must be protected to avoid unauthorized
  access or data breaches.

- **Data consistency:** AI agents need to access and process data in
  real time, meaning they must interact seamlessly with existing
  databases and services. Ensuring data consistency and synchronization
  between AI systems and traditional enterprise applications is vital
  for operational reliability.[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm23}

- **Data contracts:** Often, legacy systems do not have the same data
  structures or formats that AI systems require. Standardized data
  contracts between the enterprise systems and AI agents ensure smooth
  data flow without data corruption or loss of information.
:::
::::
:::::
::::::

:::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec10 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec10Heading"}
#### [2.1.3.2 ]{.HeadingNumber}Context and State Management {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec10Heading .Heading}

[Context and state management]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm24} are
essential for AI agents to understand and act on information
effectively. An agent's decisions often depend on both current
interactions (short-term memory) and past events (long-term memory).
Managing these states while balancing performance, cost, and data
freshness is a key architectural challenge.

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec11 .section .Section4 .RenderAsSection4 aria-labelledby="Sec11Heading"}
##### [2.1.3.2.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Key Considerations {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec11Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par53 .Para}
::: UnorderedList
- []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB44 .pagebreak aria-label="44"
  role="doc-pagebreak" title="44"}[**Short-term
  memory**]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm25}**:** This typically
  involves tracking session-based data, such as active conversations or
  recent interactions with the system. Maintaining low-latency access to
  this data is crucial for real-time decision-making.

- **Long-term memory:** [Long-term
  memory]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm26} usually involves storing
  historical data, such as past interactions or decisions, which can be
  retrieved for context in future interactions. Implementing vector
  stores for semantic retrieval allows the agent to access past
  knowledge in a meaningful way. However, keeping this data updated and
  relevant adds another layer of complexity, particularly when balancing
  performance and storage costs.

- [**Data freshness vs.
  cost**]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm27}**:** Storing and
  processing large amounts of memory over time can be expensive.
  Balancing the need for real-time data access with the costs of keeping
  data fresh in long-term storage is a critical challenge, particularly
  when dealing with large-scale enterprise
  systems.[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm28}
:::
::::
:::::
::::::

:::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec12 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec12Heading"}
#### [2.1.3.3 ]{.HeadingNumber}Governance and Control {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec12Heading .Heading}

In highly regulated environments, ensuring that AI agents comply with
security policies, legal frameworks, and industry regulations is
crucial. Enterprises need to have [governance and
control]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm29} measures in place to
prevent the AI system from violating regulations or causing harm.

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec13 .section .Section4 .RenderAsSection4 aria-labelledby="Sec13Heading"}
##### [2.1.3.3.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Key Considerations {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec13Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par58 .Para}
::: UnorderedList
- []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB45 .pagebreak aria-label="45"
  role="doc-pagebreak" title="45"}**Policy engines:** AI agents must
  operate within defined rules that govern their actions. These rules
  may pertain to security, business logic, or regulatory compliance
  (such as GDPR or the EU AI Act). Policy engines are used to enforce
  these rules, ensuring that AI agents only perform actions that align
  with corporate and legal
  expectations.[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm30}

- **Human-in-the-loop escalation:** For critical decisions, especially
  those that are ambiguous or potentially risky, AI agents should
  escalate them to human reviewers or specialized agents. This
  [human-in-the-loop process]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm31}
  ensures that decisions affecting customers or operations are made by
  responsible parties rather than being solely automated.

- **Audit trails:** Immutable logs of AI system activities are essential
  for maintaining compliance. These logs track each decision the agent
  makes, its reasoning process, and the data it uses, providing full
  transparency for regulatory audits.
:::
::::
:::::
::::::

:::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec14 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec14Heading"}
#### [2.1.3.4 ]{.HeadingNumber}Observability and Debugging {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec14Heading .Heading}

Given the complexity of Agentic AI systems, [debugging and
monitoring]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm32} them presents unique
challenges. Unlike traditional systems, where the flow of execution is
predictable, agentic systems can behave unpredictably due to their
reliance on dynamic decision-making and learning.

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec15 .section .Section4 .RenderAsSection4 aria-labelledby="Sec15Heading"}
##### [2.1.3.4.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Key Considerations {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec15Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par63 .Para}
::: UnorderedList
- []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB46 .pagebreak aria-label="46"
  role="doc-pagebreak" title="46"}**End-to-end tracing:** To debug AI
  systems effectively, enterprises need to trace the entire flow of data
  and decisions. This includes tracing prompts to language models, tool
  invocations, and data queries. Tools like OpenTelemetry enable
  [end-to-end tracing]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm33}, providing
  full visibility into how the AI agent reaches its conclusions.

- **Behavior replays:** Sometimes, it's necessary to replay specific
  actions or sessions to understand how the agent arrived at a
  particular decision. Capturing execution graphs allows teams to
  "replay" past behavior, helping them identify where something went
  wrong or why a decision was made.

- [**Reasoning
  visualizations**]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm34}**:** Visual
  tools that map the decision-making process of AI agents can be
  valuable for understanding how and why certain decisions were made.
  These visualizations can show action trees, confidence scores, and
  prompt histories, providing engineers with clear insights into agent
  behavior.
:::
::::
:::::
::::::

:::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec16 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec16Heading"}
#### [2.1.3.5 ]{.HeadingNumber}Performance and Cost Optimization {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec16Heading .Heading}

AI systems, particularly those using [large language models
(LLMs)]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm35}, can be computationally
expensive to run at scale. Managing both performance and
[cost]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm36} requires a strategic
approach to selecting the appropriate models and execution patterns.

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec17 .section .Section4 .RenderAsSection4 aria-labelledby="Sec17Heading"}
##### [2.1.3.5.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Key Considerations {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec17Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par68 .Para}
::: UnorderedList
- []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB47 .pagebreak aria-label="47"
  role="doc-pagebreak" title="47"}**Tiered model selection:** Not every
  task requires the same level of sophistication. For routine tasks that
  don't require advanced decision-making, smaller, less expensive LLMs
  can be used. For more complex decisions that could impact the
  business, premium models can be deployed. This tiered approach ensures
  that performance meets the required standards without overspending on
  processing costs.

- [**Latency-aware
  orchestration**]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm37}**:** Many AI
  applications require quick responses to be effective. It's essential
  to consider the latency of model calls and other operations in the
  architecture. Latency-aware orchestration optimizes the sequence in
  which tasks are executed, ensuring that time-sensitive decisions are
  made promptly without overloading the system.

- [**Service-level agreements
  (SLAs)**]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm38}**:** Aligning the AI
  architecture with organizational SLAs ensures that performance
  requirements are met while staying within the company's budget. This
  may involve adjusting the complexity of models or implementing
  execution patterns that reduce resource consumption.
:::
::::
:::::
::::::

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec18 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec18Heading"}
#### [2.1.3.6 ]{.HeadingNumber}Best Practice Checklist {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec18Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par72 .Para}
To ensure successful implementation and scalability, enterprises should
follow these best practices:

::: UnorderedList
- [**Map data flows**]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm39}**:**
  Clearly define how data will flow between language models, vector
  stores, and APIs, ensuring that data is processed efficiently and
  consistently.

- []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB48 .pagebreak aria-label="48"
  role="doc-pagebreak" title="48"}**Define** [**escalation
  thresholds**]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm40}**:** Set clear
  rules for when AI agents should escalate decisions to human reviewers
  or other agents to avoid potential risks or errors.

- **Implement telemetry:** Implement unified
  [telemetry]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm41} to track and log
  reasoning and action loops. This provides insight into agent behavior
  and helps with debugging, optimization, and compliance monitoring.

- **Select a framework:** Choose a
  [framework]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm42} (such as LangGraph,
  AutoGen, or CrewAI) that integrates smoothly with your CI/CD pipeline.
  This ensures that the agent's development and deployment processes are
  aligned with enterprise standards for continuous integration and
  delivery.
:::
::::
:::::
::::::::::::::::::::::::::
::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::

::::::::::::::::::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec19 .section .Section1 .RenderAsSection1 aria-labelledby="Sec19Heading"}
## [2.2 ]{.HeadingNumber}Foundational Building Blocks {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec19Heading .Heading}

In architecting Agentic AI systems, it's crucial to establish robust
building blocks to ensure that the system can ingest, reason, and act on
data reliably and efficiently. These [foundational
elements]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm43} lay the groundwork for
scaling AI-driven decisions within an enterprise. Below are the core
components of such systems, each addressing a distinct part of the AI
workflow.

:::::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec20 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec20Heading"}
### [2.2.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Perception: Ingesting and Validating Inputs {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec20Heading .Heading}

The first step in any Agentic AI system is the reliable intake of raw
data from diverse sources. For enterprise-grade systems, the [perception
layer]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm44} must be capable of handling
high volumes of varied input data while ensuring that quality,
relevance, and security are maintained.

::::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec21 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec21Heading"}
#### [2.2.1.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Key Considerations {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec21Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par79 .Para}
::: UnorderedList
- []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB49 .pagebreak aria-label="49"
  role="doc-pagebreak" title="49"}**Support diverse channels:** AI
  agents need to process inputs from multiple sources: natural language
  queries, sensor telemetry, API payloads, and event streams. A
  perception layer must handle these various formats and allow for
  seamless integration with different data streams.

- **Enforce data quality:** Data validation is critical to ensure that
  only relevant, high-quality data is passed through to the reasoning
  layer. Implementing schema checks, rate limiting mechanisms, anomaly
  detection algorithms, and sanitization processes helps filter out
  irrelevant or malicious data that could disrupt the system's
  decision-making.

- **Preprocess at scale:** To handle large volumes of incoming data
  efficiently, preprocessing tasks such as tokenization, normalization,
  feature extraction, and embedding generation must be performed at
  scale. A distributed pipeline---such as Apache Flink or Spark
  Streaming---can be used to scale these processes, ensuring that the
  system can process high-throughput data in real time.
:::
::::

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_FPar1 .FormalPara .FormalParaRenderingStyle1 .ParaTypeImportant}
::: Heading
*Enterprise Tip*
:::

*To manage scalability and back pressure effectively, decouple the
ingestion layer from downstream processing by implementing a message
broker (e.g., Kafka, RabbitMQ). This ensures that incoming data is
handled asynchronously, with mechanisms in place to handle slowdowns or
surges in traffic.*
::::
:::::::
::::::::

:::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec22 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec22Heading"}
### [2.2.2 ]{.HeadingNumber}Reasoning: Hypotheses, Trade-Offs, and Decision Logic {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec22Heading .Heading}

[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB50 .pagebreak aria-label="50"
role="doc-pagebreak" title="50"}Once the data is ingested, the AI system
must reason through the information to generate potential actions. This
is where [hypothesis generation]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm45},
trade-off analysis, and decision-making take place. The reasoning layer
is central to how the AI evaluates situations and determines the optimal
course of action.

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec23 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec23Heading"}
#### [2.2.2.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Key Considerations {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec23Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par85 .Para}
::: UnorderedList
- **Hypothesis generation:** The agent generates possible hypotheses or
  actions based on the input data. This may be achieved through
  prompt-based templates or programmatic routines that invoke [large
  language models (LLMs)]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm46} to
  generate potential responses or actions. This phase can involve
  examining past interactions or real-time data to predict the best
  possible solution.

- [**Trade-off scoring**]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm47}**:**
  Once a set of possible actions has been generated, the AI needs to
  evaluate these alternatives against predefined criteria. These
  criteria may include cost, latency, risk, compliance, or business
  impact. Scoring alternatives helps prioritize the most favorable
  options for execution.

- **Decision policy engine:** The [decision policy
  engine]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm48} applies business rules,
  reinforcement learning (RL) policies, or other mechanisms like
  multi-armed bandits to select the most appropriate action. The policy
  engine ensures that decisions are made in a consistent and predictable
  manner, aligning with the organization's strategic goals and
  regulatory requirements.
:::
::::

*To ensure transparency and auditability, embed decision criteria
directly in both prompts and policy tables. This allows stakeholders to
trace how decisions were made, providing accountability for every action
taken by the system.*
:::::
::::::

:::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec24 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec24Heading"}
### [2.2.3 ]{.HeadingNumber}Action: Orchestrating Tools and Environments {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec24Heading .Heading}

[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB51 .pagebreak aria-label="51"
role="doc-pagebreak" title="51"}Once a decision has been made, the AI
system must execute it effectively. The [action
layer]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm49} ensures that decisions are
translated into reliable, scalable operations. This layer involves
selecting the right tools, executing actions in a controlled manner, and
handling outcomes.

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec25 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec25Heading"}
#### [2.2.3.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Key Considerations {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec25Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par91 .Para}
::: UnorderedList
- **Tool selection:** Depending on the decision made, the agent must
  dynamically choose the correct API endpoint, microservice, or on-chain
  contract to execute the action. This flexibility ensures that the
  right []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm50}resource is used for the
  right task.

- **Execution patterns:** To maintain consistency and reliability,
  action execution should follow robust transactional semantics.
  Techniques such as retries with exponential back-off, idempotent
  calls, and the use of eventual consistency mechanisms help ensure that
  actions are executed reliably even in the face of failures or retries.

- []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB52 .pagebreak aria-label="52"
  role="doc-pagebreak" title="52"}**Outcome handling:** After executing
  an action, the system must process the results, manage exceptions, and
  feed status updates back into the agent's context store. This feedback
  loop is crucial for tracking the progress of tasks and updating the
  system\'s understanding of the current state.
:::
::::

**Enterprise Insight:** For actions that can significantly impact
downstream systems (e.g., financial settlements, production
deployments), leverage circuit breakers and canary deployments to
mitigate risks. These mechanisms help ensure that potentially damaging
operations are carefully monitored and controlled.
:::::
::::::

:::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec26 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec26Heading"}
### [2.2.4 ]{.HeadingNumber}Integration Layer: APIs, Data Platforms, and Event Buses {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec26Heading .Heading}

The [integration layer]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm51} serves as
the backbone of Agentic AI systems, connecting the perception,
reasoning, and action layers. A resilient and scalable integration layer
ensures that the components work together seamlessly while maintaining
flexibility and performance.

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec27 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec27Heading"}
#### [2.2.4.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Key Considerations {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec27Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par97 .Para}
::: UnorderedList
- **API gateway:** Centralize key functions such as authentication,
  authorization, rate limiting, and request routing through an
  [API]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm52} gateway. This ensures that
  all incoming requests are properly validated and routed to the
  appropriate components.

- **Data platforms:** Combining real-time data lakes, vector search
  services, and time-series databases provides a robust infrastructure
  to support both short-term and long-term memory requirements. These
  []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB53 .pagebreak aria-label="53"
  role="doc-pagebreak" title="53"}platforms store and manage data across
  various time frames, enabling agents to make decisions based on both
  immediate context and historical knowledge.

- **Event-driven architecture:** Event-driven architecture is crucial
  for maintaining scalability and decoupling components in the system.
  Using event buses such as Kafka or AWS EventBridge allows
  asynchronous, loosely coupled communication, ensuring that different
  parts of the system can operate independently while maintaining a
  unified workflow. Additionally, [event-driven
  systems]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm53} help provide an
  immutable audit trail for regulatory and compliance purposes.
:::
::::

***Best Practice:*** *Align your integration layer with your
organization's existing service mesh and observability standards. By
doing so, you can unify logging, metrics, and tracing across all
components of the Agentic AI system, ensuring consistent monitoring and
troubleshooting capabilities.*
:::::
::::::
:::::::::::::::::::::

::::::::::::::::::::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec28 .section .Section1 .RenderAsSection1 aria-labelledby="Sec28Heading"}
## [2.3 ]{.HeadingNumber}End-to-End Agentic Workflows {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec28Heading .Heading}

Agentic AI systems derive their strength from tightly integrated
workflows that are iterative, goal-driven, and self-improving. At the
heart of these systems lies a [structured
loop]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm54}: **Plan, Execute, Learn**.
This architecture enables agents not only to perform tasks but to refine
their strategies based on outcomes, context changes, and
feedback---moving beyond automation toward adaptive intelligence.

<figure id="Fig2" class="Figure">
<div id="631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_MO2" class="MediaObject">
<img src="images/631522_1_En_2_Chapter/631522_1_En_2_Fig2_HTML.jpg"
class="ImageStyle3"
alt="Flow chart illustrating &quot;Agentic Workflows: Key Design Patterns.&quot; Central box connects to four sub-boxes: &quot;Reflection&quot; (reviews output), &quot;Tool Usage&quot; (interacts with tools), &quot;Planning&quot; (breaks down goals), and &quot;Multi-Agent Collaboration&quot; (collaborates with agents). Each sub-box describes a specific design pattern." />
</div>
<figcaption><div class="CaptionContent">
<span class="CaptionNumber">Figure 2-2</span>
<p>Key design patterns in agentic workflows</p>
</div></figcaption>
</figure>

[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB54 .pagebreak aria-label="54"
role="doc-pagebreak" title="54"}This diagram illustrates core [design
patterns]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm55} that support the
Plan--Execute--Learn cycle in agentic systems. These include planning
(breaking goals into tasks), tool usage (interfacing with external
systems), reflection (self-evaluation of outputs), and multi-agent
collaboration (delegating tasks across specialized agents). Together,
these patterns enable dynamic, iterative workflows central to effective
Agentic AI.

::::::::::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec29 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec29Heading"}
### [2.3.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Plan → Execute → Learn Feedback Loop {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec29Heading .Heading}

Agentic AI systems thrive on the iterative loop of
[planning]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm56}, executing, and
learning. This feedback loop enables agents to adapt, refine their
actions, and optimize performance based on real-world outcomes.

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec30 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec30Heading"}
#### [2.3.1.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Plan Phase {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec30Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par105 .Para}
::: UnorderedList
- **Goal decomposition:** The first step is breaking down the high-level
  objective into manageable tasks or milestones. This step ensures that
  the agent has a clear roadmap for execution, aligning the complexity
  of the overall goal with smaller, actionable steps.

- **Resource allocation:** Assigning compute resources, selecting
  appropriate LLM variants, and provisioning necessary external tools or
  APIs are key to ensuring that the agent has the right capabilities and
  resources at each stage of the process.

- []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB55 .pagebreak aria-label="55"
  role="doc-pagebreak" title="55"}**Strategy formulation:** This phase
  involves developing a strategy using prompt templates or policy
  modules. By incorporating past performance data, the agent formulates
  potential action sequences to achieve the defined goals. This ensures
  that each action is planned based on the agent's accumulated
  knowledge.
:::
::::
:::::

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec31 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec31Heading"}
#### [2.3.1.2 ]{.HeadingNumber}Execute Phase {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec31Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par109 .Para}
::: UnorderedList
- **Stepwise action:** The [agent]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm57}
  performs the tasks sequentially, invoking tools or APIs in the
  prescribed order. Each action is designed to be idempotent and
  resilient, ensuring that retries or back-offs occur without breaking
  the flow.

- **Interim validation:** After each subtask, lightweight checks---such
  as schema conformance and basic business rules---are applied to detect
  any early signs of drift or anomalies. This helps maintain quality and
  ensures the agent stays on track.

- **Context enrichment:** As actions are executed, the agent enriches
  its context store with new outcomes and observations. This data is
  stored in the session state or vector store, creating a record of the
  agent's decision-making process for future use.
:::
::::
:::::

:::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec32 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec32Heading"}
#### [2.3.1.3 ]{.HeadingNumber}Learn Phase {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec32Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par113 .Para}
::: UnorderedList
- **Outcome analysis:** After completing the execution
  [phase]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm58}, the agent compares the
  actual results with the planned targets, evaluating metrics such as
  time to completion, cost, and accuracy. This analysis highlights areas
  where the system succeeded or fell short.

- []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB56 .pagebreak aria-label="56"
  role="doc-pagebreak" title="56"}**Feedback injection:** Performance
  gaps identified in the outcome analysis feed directly back into the
  system. This can involve adjusting prompt weights, fine-tuning
  decision thresholds, or updating policy tables to refine future
  actions.

- **Model calibration:** Over time, agents can leverage reinforcement
  learning signals or human annotations to further calibrate their
  models, gradually improving their decision-making and ensuring that
  the agent adapts to changing circumstances.
:::
::::

::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par117 .Para}
> *By closing the loop---planning, executing, and learning---agents
> evolve from one-off scripts into adaptive, self-improving systems.*
:::
::::::
:::::::::::::

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec33 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec33Heading"}
### [2.3.2 ]{.HeadingNumber}Human in the Loop: Escalation and Guardrails {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec33Heading .Heading}

Even the most sophisticated agentic systems require oversight,
especially in high-stakes situations where errors could have significant
consequences. A layered approach ensures that safety and compliance are
maintained []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm59}throughout the
process.

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par120 .Para}
::: UnorderedList
- [**Threshold-based
  escalation**]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm60}**:** Define
  quantitative triggers---such as a confidence score below 0.7 or cost
  exceeding budget---that automatically escalate the task to a human
  operator or secondary "LLM judge." This ensures that critical
  decisions are reviewed before execution, especially when the agent\'s
  confidence is low.

- []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB57 .pagebreak aria-label="57"
  role="doc-pagebreak" title="57"}**LLM judge mechanism:** Deploy a
  lightweight, specialized model to review or veto key decisions---like
  financial transactions or regulatory filings---before the agent
  executes them. This additional layer provides an important safeguard
  against potentially harmful or non-compliant actions.

- **Approval workflows:** Integrate with ticketing or workflow engines
  (e.g., Jira, ServiceNow) to queue tasks for human review and sign-off.
  These workflows should come with audit trails and time-stamped
  decisions to maintain transparency and accountability.

- **Dynamic**
  [**guardrails**]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm61}**:** Implement
  runtime policy checks to ensure that actions align with organizational
  guidelines, data usage policies, and compliance rules. These
  guardrails should be adjustable centrally, without requiring
  redeployment of the agent, to remain flexible in a dynamic regulatory
  environment.

- **Enterprise Insight:** "Balance autonomy with control: let the agent
  handle routine steps, but reserve human review for exceptions and edge
  cases."
:::
::::
:::::

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec34 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec34Heading"}
### [2.3.3 ]{.HeadingNumber}Monitoring and Metrics: Task Completion, Latency, Accuracy {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec34Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par126 .Para}
In Agentic AI, measurable and observable performance is crucial. The
ability to track, analyze, and optimize the agent's behavior in real
time is essential for ensuring high standards and meeting [service-level
agreements
(SLAs)]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm62}.[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB58
.pagebreak aria-label="58" role="doc-pagebreak" title="58"}

::: UnorderedList
- [**Real-time
  instrumentation**]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm63}**:** Trace
  every reasoning step, tool call, and data fetch using distributed
  tracing frameworks like OpenTelemetry. This comprehensive tracing
  provides visibility into the agent's processes and helps identify
  areas for improvement or optimization.

- [**Post-mortem analysis**]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm64}**:**
  Capture complete "replay logs" for each agent run. These logs include
  prompts, intermediate states, and actions taken, providing a detailed
  record that can be used for root cause analysis during
  troubleshooting. This enables teams to understand exactly what
  happened during a run and how to improve the system in the future.

- [**Alerts and thresholds**]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm65}**:**
  Set up automated alerts (via tools like Slack or PagerDuty) for SLA
  breaches---such as sustained latency spikes or increasing error rates.
  These alerts ensure that the right stakeholders are notified
  immediately, allowing quick corrective action to be taken.
:::
::::
:::::

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec35 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec35Heading"}
### [2.3.4 ]{.HeadingNumber}Best Practice Checklist {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec35Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par130 .Para}
::: UnorderedList
- Establish [baseline]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm66} performance
  in a staging environment before production rollout.

- Continuously compare live metrics against benchmarks and adjust
  resource allocations dynamically.

- Regularly audit "replay logs" to uncover hidden failure modes and
  refine decision policies.
:::
::::
:::::
:::::::::::::::::::::::

:::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec36 .section .Section1 .RenderAsSection1 aria-labelledby="Sec36Heading"}
## [2.4 ]{.HeadingNumber}Proven Design Patterns {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec36Heading .Heading}

[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB59 .pagebreak aria-label="59"
role="doc-pagebreak" title="59"}In this section, we delve into [proven
design patterns]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm67} that have become
the backbone of effective Agentic AI systems. These patterns enable
agents to function with precision, adaptability, and scalability. We
begin with ReAct (Reason--Action
[Cycles]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm68}), a fundamental approach
where agents continuously iterate through reasoning and action, refining
their behavior with each cycle. By adopting these patterns, you can
build agents that not only perform tasks but evolve and improve through
each interaction.

:::::::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec37 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec37Heading"}
### [2.4.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}ReAct (Reason--Action Cycles) {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec37Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par135 .Para}
The **ReAct** pattern emphasizes continuous decision-making by embedding
a tight "think--do" cycle in the core functionality of an agent. This
allows agents to operate iteratively and adjust their actions based on
real-time observations. The [loop
functions]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm69} as follows:

::: OrderedList
1.  ::: ItemNumber
    1\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    **Observe:** The agent starts by assessing the current environment,
    including input from users, APIs, or other sources. This observation
    step provides the context necessary for the agent to understand its
    environment.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

2.  ::: ItemNumber
    2\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    **Think:** Using the observed data, the agent generates hypotheses,
    makes predictions, or identifies subgoals by issuing prompts to an
    LLM (large language [model]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm70}).
    This is where the agent's reasoning capabilities come into play,
    exploring possible paths forward.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

3.  ::: ItemNumber
    3\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    **Act:** Based on the reasoning step, the agent makes decisions
    about the next best action, which could involve invoking an API,
    triggering an external service, or taking an internal action based
    on predefined rules.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

4.  ::: ItemNumber
    4\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB60 .pagebreak aria-label="60"
    role="doc-pagebreak" title="60"}**Review:** Once the action has been
    executed, the agent evaluates the result. This review step includes
    verifying if the expected outcome has been achieved and integrating
    the results into the agent's context. This information is used to
    refine future decisions and improve the reasoning process.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::
:::
::::

<figure id="Fig3" class="Figure">
<div id="631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_MO3" class="MediaObject">
<img src="images/631522_1_En_2_Chapter/631522_1_En_2_Fig3_HTML.jpg"
class="ImageStyle3"
alt="Flow chart illustrating a process loop. It begins with &quot;Input Trigger,&quot; leading to &quot;Reasoning,&quot; followed by &quot;Action Phase.&quot; The process repeats until the &quot;desired outcome is achieved,&quot; then proceeds to &quot;Output/Action.&quot; Arrows indicate the flow direction between each step." />
</div>
<figcaption><div class="CaptionContent">
<span class="CaptionNumber">Figure 2-3</span>
<p>ReAct <span
id="631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm71">workflow</span></p>
</div></figcaption>
</figure>

This cyclic pattern enables agents to adapt to unforeseen circumstances
or evolving tasks. It dramatically reduces errors, particularly in
multi-step tasks, where intermediate decisions may influence the final
outcome. The integration of feedback within each cycle enhances
adaptability and reduces the occurrence of hallucinations---when the
agent produces incorrect or misleading results.

::::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec38 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec38Heading"}
#### [2.4.1.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Key Benefits {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec38Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par141 .Para}
::: UnorderedList
- Real-time self-correction

- Minimizes errors and hallucinations

- [Facilitates]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm72} handling dynamic,
  multi-step tasks
:::
::::

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_FPar2 .FormalPara .FormalParaRenderingStyle1 .ParaTypeImportant}
::: Heading
*Developer Tip*
:::

*Format prompts with clear "Thought:" and "Action:" markers, and use a
termination token (e.g., DONE) to signal when an objective is met. This
increases transparency and helps in debugging.*
::::
:::::::
::::::::::

:::::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec39 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec39Heading"}
### [2.4.2 ]{.HeadingNumber}Hierarchical and Composite Agents {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec39Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par146 .Para}
[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB61 .pagebreak aria-label="61"
role="doc-pagebreak" title="61"}As tasks become more complex, relying on
a single agent to handle all operations can become inefficient or
impractical. In such cases, **hierarchical and composite
agent**[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm73} architectures are
employed. The architecture is based on the principle of **task
decomposition** and involves a primary agent (Root Orchestrator)
delegating tasks to specialized sub-agents, each handling a specific
subset of the larger problem.

::: OrderedList
1.  ::: ItemNumber
    1\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    **Root Orchestrator:** The high-level agent that accepts a complex,
    broad objective and breaks it down into smaller, manageable tasks.
    The Root Orchestrator coordinates the entire process, ensuring the
    sub-agents operate cohesively toward the overall goal.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

2.  ::: ItemNumber
    2\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    **Specialized sub-agents:** These are focused agents, each
    responsible for a specific domain or task. For example, one
    sub-agent might handle data retrieval, another might focus on
    processing analytics, and yet another might handle transaction
    execution. Each sub-agent is designed to operate autonomously within
    its specialized scope.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

3.  ::: ItemNumber
    3\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB62 .pagebreak aria-label="62"
    role="doc-pagebreak" title="62"}**Aggregation layer:** After the
    sub-agents complete their tasks, their outputs are sent to an
    aggregation layer that reconciles, integrates, and resolves any
    conflicts between the sub-agent results. The final output is
    composed and delivered as the result of the entire system's work.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::
:::
::::

This pattern is particularly beneficial in scenarios where tasks grow
too large or complex for a single agent to manage efficiently. By
splitting responsibilities across agents, teams can independently scale
and test each agent, much like microservices in traditional software
architecture.

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec40 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec40Heading"}
#### [2.4.2.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Key Benefits {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec40Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par151 .Para}
::: UnorderedList
- Decomposes complex tasks []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm74}into
  manageable subtasks

- Allows independent development and testing of each agent

- Scalable and modular approach akin to microservices
:::
::::

***Consideration**: Clear* ***data contracts*** *between agents and the*
***error propagation*** *policies are crucial. A failure in one agent
should trigger compensatory actions in other agents to prevent cascading
failures.*
:::::
::::::::

:::::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec41 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec41Heading"}
### [2.4.3 ]{.HeadingNumber}Multi-agent Coordination Frameworks {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec41Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par156 .Para}
In more complex enterprise applications, [**multi-agent
coordination**]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm75} frameworks enable
numerous agents to collaborate and work toward a shared goal. This is
especially useful in distributed systems like **global supply chain
optimization** or **distributed customer support**.

::: OrderedList
1.  ::: ItemNumber
    1\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    **Communication bus:** A central messaging system (e.g., Kafka, AWS
    EventBridge) allows agents to exchange information and updates
    asynchronously. []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB63 .pagebreak
    aria-label="63" role="doc-pagebreak" title="63"}The bus ensures that
    agents can communicate their intents, share progress, and pass data
    between each other without needing direct, synchronous connections.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

2.  ::: ItemNumber
    2\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    **Consensus protocols:** When multiple agents are working on a
    shared task, maintaining consistency and truth across the system is
    crucial. Consensus protocols such as **leader election** or **voting
    rounds** ensure that there is a single source of truth and that
    decisions are agreed upon by the participating agents.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

3.  ::: ItemNumber
    3\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    **Dynamic task allocation:** With multiple agents working on
    different parts of a problem, **dynamic task allocation** ensures
    that tasks are matched with the most suitable agent. For example, an
    agent specializing in data processing might be allocated tasks
    involving heavy data manipulation, while a more general-purpose
    agent handles user interactions.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

4.  ::: ItemNumber
    4\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    **Collaboration and negotiation:** In scenarios where no single
    agent has complete data or capabilities, agents collaborate,
    negotiate handoffs, and contribute their expertise to the overall
    solution. This decentralized collaboration is often referred to as
    **peer-to-peer coordination**.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::
:::

[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB64 .pagebreak aria-label="64"
role="doc-pagebreak" title="64"}
::::

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec42 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec42Heading"}
#### [2.4.3.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Key Benefits {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec42Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par161 .Para}
::: UnorderedList
- Facilitates collaboration between multiple agents to solve complex
  problems

- Scales effectively across distributed systems

- Helps when no single agent has full context
:::
::::

***Consideration**: Ensure* ***robust logging*** *of inter-agent
messages and* ***secure communication*** *using protocols like*
***mutual TLS*** *to safeguard both traceability and security.*
:::::
::::::::

:::::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec43 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec43Heading"}
### [2.4.4 ]{.HeadingNumber}Tool-Enhanced Agents (Swappable Connectors) {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec43Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par166 .Para}
Enterprise agents often need to interact with various back-end systems
and services, which may change over time. The **Tool-Enhanced Agent**
[pattern]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm76} offers a flexible and
resilient way to integrate with these external systems through dynamic
**connector swapping**.

::: OrderedList
1.  ::: ItemNumber
    1\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    **Connector registry:** This registry serves as a map, linking
    abstract agent commands (like
    [fetch_invoice]{.EmphasisFontCategoryNonProportional}) to concrete
    APIs, SDK functions, or service calls. When the agent needs to
    perform an action, it queries the registry and binds to the
    appropriate connector based on the context.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

2.  ::: ItemNumber
    2\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    **Runtime connector binding:** The agent dynamically selects the
    correct connector at runtime. For example, it might choose an API to
    interact with SAP for billing or switch to a legacy microservice for
    inventory updates. This enables the agent to operate across diverse
    back-end systems without needing to hard-code dependencies.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

3.  ::: ItemNumber
    3\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB65 .pagebreak aria-label="65"
    role="doc-pagebreak" title="65"}**Fallback strategies:** To ensure
    resilience, the agent implements fallback mechanisms. If the primary
    connector fails, the agent automatically retries the request using
    an alternative connector, ensuring continuous operation without
    disruption.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

4.  ::: ItemNumber
    4\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    **Health checks and versioning:** Connectors are versioned to handle
    compatibility with different system versions. Health checks are also
    in place to monitor the status of connectors, alerting the system
    when a connector is unavailable or needs maintenance.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::
:::
::::

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec44 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec44Heading"}
#### [2.4.4.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Key Benefits {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec44Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par171 .Para}
::: UnorderedList
- Enables seamless integration with diverse back-end systems

- Increases resilience through fallback mechanisms

- Provides flexibility to update or swap out connectors as needed
:::
::::

***Consideration**: Ensure connectors are dynamically loaded without
requiring code changes. This allows easy updates or replacements of
back-end systems without disrupting the agent\'s operation.*
:::::
::::::::

:::::::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec45 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec45Heading"}
### [2.4.5 ]{.HeadingNumber}ReAct + RAG: Combining Reasoning, Action, and Real-Time Knowledge Retrieval {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec45Heading .Heading}

[ReAct + RAG agents]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm77} represent an
advanced evolution of the traditional **ReAct** cycle. These agents not
only engage in reasoning and
[action]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm78}, but also dynamically
access external sources of knowledge, allowing them to
[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB66 .pagebreak aria-label="66"
role="doc-pagebreak" title="66"}make well-informed decisions grounded in
real-time, domain-specific data. This combination of reasoning, action,
and knowledge retrieval makes them ideal for high-stakes or
precision-critical tasks where accurate, up-to-date information is key.

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec46 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec46Heading"}
#### [2.4.5.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}How ReAct + RAG Works {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec46Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par177 .Para}
The **ReAct + RAG** agent operates by alternating between three [core
phases]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm79}: **reasoning**,
**knowledge retrieval**, and **action**. This workflow ensures the agent
is continually accessing relevant, up-to-date data, allowing it to make
informed decisions that reflect the most current state of knowledge
available. Here\'s a breakdown of the process:

::: UnorderedList
- **Input query:** The agent begins by receiving a query or task that
  needs to be addressed.

- **Reasoning phase:** The agent processes the query by analyzing it and
  breaking it down into manageable steps or hypotheses that guide its
  next actions.

- **Knowledge retrieval:** During this phase, the agent pulls in
  relevant, real-time data from external sources, such as APIs,
  databases, knowledge bases, or documentation. This ensures the agent
  is using the most current information available.

- **Action phase:** Based on the insights gained from the knowledge
  retrieval phase, the agent executes an action, whether it's calling an
  API, triggering an event, or making a decision.

- [**Iteration**]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm80}**:** If the
  initial action does not resolve the task or query, the agent continues
  iterating through the reasoning and knowledge retrieval phases,
  refining its understanding and actions until the desired outcome is
  achieved.
:::
::::

<figure id="Fig4" class="Figure">
<div id="631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_MO4" class="MediaObject">
<img src="images/631522_1_En_2_Chapter/631522_1_En_2_Fig4_HTML.jpg"
class="ImageStyle3"
alt="Flow chart titled &quot;ReAct + RAG Agent&quot; illustrating a process. It begins with &quot;Input Query,&quot; leading to &quot;Reasoning.&quot; The process continues to &quot;Knowledge Retrieval,&quot; then &quot;Output/Action.&quot; A loop connects &quot;Action Phase&quot; back to &quot;Reasoning,&quot; indicating repetition until the desired outcome is achieved. Arrows show the flow direction between each step." />
</div>
<figcaption><div class="CaptionContent">
<span class="CaptionNumber">Figure 2-4</span>
<p>ReAct + RAG agent</p>
</div></figcaption>
</figure>

[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB67 .pagebreak aria-label="67"
role="doc-pagebreak" title="67"}This continuous loop of reasoning,
retrieving, and acting provides a high level of accuracy and ensures
that the agent remains grounded in the most relevant, up-to-date
information.
:::::

:::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec47 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec47Heading"}
#### [2.4.5.2 ]{.HeadingNumber}Ideal Use Cases for ReAct + RAG {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec47Heading .Heading}

The [integration]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm81} of reasoning and
knowledge retrieval in **ReAct + RAG** agents makes them particularly
suited for tasks requiring both high precision and access to dynamic,
ever-evolving knowledge. These agents excel in domains where the
environment is constantly changing and decisions need to be based on
real-time or domain-specific data.

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec48 .section .Section4 .RenderAsSection4 aria-labelledby="Sec48Heading"}
##### [2.4.5.2.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Example Applications {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec48Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par185 .Para}
::: UnorderedList
- [**Legal research
  assistants**]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm82}**:** The agent
  accesses current legal databases to gather the most relevant case
  studies, laws, and legal opinions, reasoning through complex legal
  queries to provide precise recommendations.

- [**Medical decision support
  systems**]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm83}**:** The agent taps
  into up-to-date clinical guidelines, research papers, and patient data
  to help make informed healthcare decisions tailored to individual
  patients.

- []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB68 .pagebreak aria-label="68"
  role="doc-pagebreak" title="68"}[**Technical troubleshooting
  agents**]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm84}**:** These agents
  combine diagnostic data with real-time technical documentation to
  resolve issues efficiently and accurately.
:::
::::
:::::
::::::
::::::::::

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec49 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec49Heading"}
### [2.4.6 ]{.HeadingNumber}Summary of Proven Design Patterns {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec49Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par189 .Para}
::: UnorderedList
- **ReAct cycles:** Real-time feedback loop between reasoning and action
  to self-correct and adapt

- **Hierarchical and composite agents:** Task decomposition into
  specialized agents for scalable problem-solving

- **Multi-agent coordination:** Enables collaboration and task sharing
  between agents for distributed tasks

- **Tool-enhanced agents:** Dynamic connection to diverse back-end
  systems, ensuring adaptability and resilience

- **ReAct + RAG:** Combines the reasoning--action loop with real-time
  knowledge retrieval, enabling agents to access external data sources
  dynamically for more informed and accurate decision-making. Ideal for
  high-stakes, precision-critical tasks
:::
::::

Together, these patterns offer a powerful foundation for building
robust, scalable, and flexible Agentic AI systems that can handle
complex, dynamic environments and provide continuous improvement.
:::::
::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::::

:::::::::::::::::::::::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec50 .section .Section1 .RenderAsSection1 aria-labelledby="Sec50Heading"}
## [2.5 ]{.HeadingNumber}Memory and State Management {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec50Heading .Heading}

[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB69 .pagebreak aria-label="69"
role="doc-pagebreak" title="69"}Memory and state management are
foundational to Agentic AI's ability to perform over time and across
various contexts. Just as humans rely on both short-term and long-term
[memory]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm85} to guide their actions
and decisions, agents must also effectively manage their internal state
to maintain continuity, adapt to new inputs, and evolve their behavior.

In the realm of enterprise-grade agents, efficient memory handling
ensures that the system can remember important context, learn from past
interactions, and make informed decisions without starting from scratch
with each new task. However, this is not a simple task. Balancing the
need for immediate context with the persistence of long-term memory
requires a thoughtful strategy that accounts for factors like
consistency, freshness, and
cost.[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm86}

This section explores the key elements of **short-term context**,
**long-term memory**, and the trade-offs in managing them. By
understanding these concepts, developers can build agents that not only
remember past actions but also optimize the way they store and retrieve
information to support intelligent, context-aware decision-making.

:::::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec51 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec51Heading"}
### [2.5.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Short-Term Context (Dialog and Session State) {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec51Heading .Heading}

In Agentic AI systems, short-term context is essential for maintaining
the continuity and relevance of interactions. This "working memory"
allows agents to process and remember immediate tasks, user inputs, and
intermediate results. The agent needs to capture recent interactions to
enhance understanding and improve decision-making.

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par200 .Para}
[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB70 .pagebreak aria-label="70"
role="doc-pagebreak" title="70"}To manage [short-term
context]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm87}, you can implement the
following:

::: OrderedList
1.  ::: ItemNumber
    1\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    **Buffer dialog turns:**

    Store the last N exchanges in a **ring buffer** or **sliding
    window**, where each entry represents a turn in the conversation.
    This ensures that the agent's prompt always reflects the most recent
    context without overwhelming the system with excessive historical
    data. By limiting the context window, the agent avoids referencing
    outdated information.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

2.  ::: ItemNumber
    2\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    **Store session variables:**

    Maintain **key--value pairs** (e.g., user preferences, transaction
    IDs, last action outcomes) in a fast in-memory cache like **Redis**
    or **Memcached**. This enables the agent to access critical session
    data quickly without recalculating or re-querying for the same
    information. Such storage can also track session states, which can
    be useful for multi-turn interactions and multi-step workflows.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

3.  ::: ItemNumber
    3\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    **Manage context size:**

    Prevent the context from exceeding token limits by **pruning** or
    **summarizing** older dialog turns. Techniques like **chunking**
    (breaking long conversations into segments) or **semantic
    summarization** (condensing dialog into a more concise format while
    preserving intent) help the agent maintain relevant context without
    losing essential details. This approach optimizes both performance
    and storage.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::
:::

[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB71 .pagebreak aria-label="71"
role="doc-pagebreak" title="71"}
::::

A well-managed short-term context ensures that the agent remains on
track, provides relevant responses, and avoids making irrelevant or
contradictory statements.

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec52 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec52Heading"}
#### [2.5.1.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Key Benefits {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec52Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par208 .Para}
::: UnorderedList
- **Focus on relevance:** Keeps only pertinent information

- **Improved flow:** Prevents loss of continuity in conversations

- **Efficient resource use:** Reduces unnecessary memory consumption
:::
::::
:::::
::::::::

:::::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec53 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec53Heading"}
### [2.5.2 ]{.HeadingNumber}Long-Term Memory (Vector Stores and Knowledge Bases) {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec53Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par212 .Para}
While short-term context helps with immediate decision-making, long-term
memory enables agents to learn from past interactions and adapt to
evolving business needs. [Long-term
memory]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm88} ensures that the agent can
persist valuable insights, personalize interactions, and retrieve
enterprise knowledge over time.

::: OrderedList
1.  ::: ItemNumber
    1\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    **Vector embeddings:** Encode documents, past conversations, and
    structured records as **high-dimensional vectors** in services like
    **Pinecone** or **FAISS**. Each vector captures the semantic meaning
    of the content, enabling similarity searches that retrieve the most
    relevant memory snippets for future queries. This allows the agent
    to "remember" previous interactions, context, and user-specific data
    in a way that's computationally efficient.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

2.  ::: ItemNumber
    2\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB72 .pagebreak aria-label="72"
    role="doc-pagebreak" title="72"}**Knowledge graphs and databases:**
    Use **graph databases** (e.g., Neo4j) or **relational databases** to
    link entities such as customers, products, and policies. This
    **entity relationship modeling** enables the agent to perform
    precise, rule-based lookups, ensuring that it has the necessary
    context to make informed decisions based on historical data.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

3.  ::: ItemNumber
    3\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    **Hybrid retrieval:** Combine **vector search** with more
    traditional search techniques like **SQL queries** or **keyword
    filters** to balance recall (retrieving as many relevant results as
    possible) with precision (ensuring relevance and accuracy). This
    hybrid approach ensures that the agent's reasoning is grounded in
    trusted, up-to-date data, which is crucial in enterprise scenarios
    where accuracy is paramount.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::
:::
::::

A well-designed long-term memory layer transforms agents from
**stateless responders** into **learning partners** that improve over
time, adapting their behaviors based on previous interactions and the
evolving context of the business.

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec54 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec54Heading"}
#### [2.5.2.1 ]{.HeadingNumber}Key Benefits {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec54Heading .Heading}

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par217 .Para}
::: UnorderedList
- **Personalization:** Tailors responses and decisions based on
  historical context

- **Persistent learning:** Builds cumulative knowledge over time

- **Adaptability:** Enhances decision-making with evolving data
:::
::::
:::::
::::::::

:::::::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec55 .section .Section2 .RenderAsSection2 aria-labelledby="Sec55Heading"}
### [2.5.3 ]{.HeadingNumber}Consistency, Freshness, and Cost Trade-Offs {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec55Heading .Heading}

[]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB73 .pagebreak aria-label="73"
role="doc-pagebreak" title="73"}[Memory
systems]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm89} come with trade-offs that
require careful planning. Three competing priorities must be balanced to
ensure the agent\'s memory is both effective and sustainable:

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Par222 .Para}
::: OrderedList
1.  ::: ItemNumber
    1\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    [**Consistency:**]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm90} Ensuring
    that the agent uses a consistent snapshot of its memory throughout a
    workflow is crucial to avoid contradictions and confusion.
    **Read-through caches** or **versioned snapshots** can be employed
    to ensure that the agent operates on a coherent memory state. This
    is especially important for workflows where the agent must make a
    series of decisions based on prior states or data.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

2.  ::: ItemNumber
    2\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    **Freshness:** [Freshness]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm91}
    ensures that the agent can react quickly to new information. For
    example, when **inventory updates** or **regulatory changes** occur,
    they must be reflected immediately in the agent's memory. Techniques
    like **event-driven invalidation** or **Time-to-Live (TTL)**
    policies can be used to ensure that the memory reflects the most
    current state of affairs. However, the challenge is balancing
    **timeliness** against the computational cost of constantly updating
    memory.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::

3.  ::: ItemNumber
    3\.
    :::

    ::: ItemContent
    [**Cost efficiency:**]{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm92} Memory
    systems are not free---vector indexing, embedding computations, and
    database queries incur operational costs. A **tiered storage
    strategy** can be used to mitigate this. **Cold archives** (for less
    frequently accessed data) and []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_PB74
    .pagebreak aria-label="74" role="doc-pagebreak" title="74"}**hot
    caches** (for frequently accessed data) can help optimize costs.
    Additionally, scheduling **off-peak batch updates** ensures that
    less time-sensitive data is updated
    []{#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_ITerm93}during low-demand periods.
    :::

    ::: ClearBoth
     
    :::
:::
::::

:::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_FPar3 .FormalPara .FormalParaRenderingStyle1 .ParaTypeImportant}
::: Heading
*Design Tip*
:::

*Define clear* ***service-level objectives (SLOs)*** *for memory latency
and freshness. If real-time decision-making is crucial (e.g., fraud
detection), invest in a* ***real-time stream processing layer*** *that
updates the memory as soon as new data arrives. For less time-sensitive
applications, periodic* ***nightly syncs*** *into the vector store may
be sufficient.*
::::

::::: {#631522_1_En_2_Chapter.xhtml_Sec56 .section .Section3 .RenderAsSection3 aria-labelledby="Sec56Heading"}
